de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the swelling of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have any hole in their ears; and this same thing happens to men through swelling of a wound, or a flesh born inside the ear, and these swellings sometimes go deep into the ear, if one cannot see them; and sometimes it happens that the hole is small and one sees them well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which goes deep, if one cannot see it, is of grievous sanitation in many dispositions, and in this you see that you must put the ear of the patient in the sun; and look within: if you see apparent opilation, if the work has all this spatium from which it is formed.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be smooth and straight in front and behind, all plain, so that it does not obstruct the ear; if the opilation is from flesh born or growth of the ear, if you hold it with subtle pincers, and lift it lightly, until this flesh is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the suppurations are deeply rooted in the ear, take a subtle and light razor and heat it slightly over the fire, then insert it into the course of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the obstruction where the patient feels great discomfort in the ear, percuss gently, and beware not to touch the nerves of the ear; then put a tent in the ear according to the width of the perforation, and the malleus in the Egyptian manner.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not leave it for a day until the wound is sewn up, or take a tent and apply gentle pressure in rose water, and sprinkle vitriol powder; and if you see the ear inflamed, it is necessary that you remove the tent and apply another gentled tent made of rose oil and wax, until the inflammation is gone; then cure until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if the flow of blood comes, plunge a sponge and wrap it in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other cures that stop the flow of blood which are or treat with distillations.
de la char des papieres	from the flesh of papyrus
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Here is the translation:
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they are without decay, if the cautery of the subtle lenticular fire is good, and the cautery operator is skilled after the incision is effective; and many times they repair, since nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, then those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the crust
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times things come in papers from the eyes that seem big in their shape and hardness, and because of this, this disease is called "grandine", and it is a gathering of much moisture above and below; the operations are such: take care that the grandine moves from one part to another, and it's a light thing to know; make then a large opening, then gently scrape each part, then take them with pincers, and cover.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	if you cannot cover it sensibly, percuss a little the paper, so as not to hurt the patient; and if the crack is large, assemble it with a bandage, and cure until it is healthy; and if it is small, do not use force, for the joints restore it quickly and with ease.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grandine descends to the depths of the ear towards the upper part, reverse the crust, and hold the grandine with pincers, and cover and press from one part to another; and if the crust is separated by incision, do not grieve anything; and when the grandine is covered, leave the salty oil, and cure the limb of what injures the flesh as long as the patient is healthy.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Here is the translation:
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press your arm to your fingers and feel the bone protruding between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient puts his head in your lap; and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains exinach from each part, then place it on them; and press with your fingers on one side and the other, so that the exinach is assembled within the circle; then make a small incision in the moisture at the sharp edge, and let it not be larger than the wound made for opening a vein; and make the skin deep enough until you reach the exinach; and in many dispositions comes exinach from the incision, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract then a piece of charpit cloth between your fingers at the defect, and turn your hand to the right and to the left until it is expanded; and beware that you do not touch in the incision, that you do not reach the entire sharp edge just up to the eye, that you do not blur it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the patient does not open at the beginning of the wound, apply a little pressure to the wound lightly so it opens; then hold steady as we have said, then wrap in soft cloth and water, and put on the limb, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who break their own arm and put it back to correct that moisture which has remained.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat until it is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess comes to the arm, then treat with emplasters soothingly until it is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When papers grow hairs unevenly other than natural, and are enveloped, they harm the eyes, and bring on ways of sickness such as accustomed tears and mollifications of the papers and albumen, so that it is a cause of destruction of the eyes; and there is a cure in three ways: either by cautery with fire altogether, or by medicine according to what is before or chapter of cautery, and it is done either by incision and stitching or by cauterization, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the patient's head in your healthy one, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, stick a needle all the way into the filament; and let it be beneath the edge of the paper where the hairs grow from those hairs, and pull the filament to the top of the paper, and turn it to the ruler; then do in the part beneath the paper, beneath the hairs aligned, all the way to the spatula, from the great hammer just to the small one; then extract the filament, and place beneath the paper a small cushion of cotton and drapery, then sign on the paper a figure of an inch, as if the leaf of myrtle, and always it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see elevated the paper which is divided into two.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if you have mastery of coping with a great quantity of paper according to how the paper is softened; then make a whole spatula-like instrument on the two lines that you have signed, and start from the great artery just a little; and let one of the fissures be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the hook in one of the two angles of the heart, then scrape everything; then assemble the two lips with a suture of a needle and the whole thread of subtle wool, and suck out the blood, and make the superfluity of the threads on the two eyebrows into all kinds of gluey things, if you want to do this; and if not, if you don't have mastery, then leave the suture and threads until three or four days; then treat the wound without suturing with dry and constricting things, for the paper revives at the suddenness of the wound and its assembly, but the suture is miserable (as the ancients said), and it's work without fear; and if there's another way: and it is that you sign the paper with a figure that is just like the leaf of myrtle, as we have recounted, three ounces of powdered form according to the shape that is here.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then apply the ointment which surmounts the small equal forces harmoniously according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you do not have the power to hold the tongs, and the thing is not equal, take a needle or thread, and insert it into the figure; and put another thread through the large artery, and the second thread through the small one, and assemble them evenly between your two hands; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin over where you have signed, as we have recounted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by suturing, and cure until it is healthy; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar ointments soothing; and never has it happened that the hairs of the papyrus are converted: so it is necessary that you use what we have said about the incision; but the suturing on one side and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of wounds is according to this form: and it is that you convert the parchment and make it thick according to what I have said, and then make artificial seams by art, and subtle threads as long as the parchment and the width of the spatula is; and apply thus the heads of the parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly above the form of the parchment of the eye, and extract the artificial seams from the formed parts; and leave them thus for some days, and the skin which is restrained will become more tender and numb and porous, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, if the wound has forces, then cure until it is healthy; and when the wound is sewn, and the papyrus is lifted, and they will no longer sprout hairs; and this is the form of the two canals that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Here is the translation:

de la porriture de l’oil	from the sight of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease which is called "aleacrati" or the porrigo arrives in the eye, there are two ways to deal with it: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from a cut, or from a cautery, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of surgery is that you make an incision, and separate the lips of it, and put in threads of linen, and bind it so it is healthy; and it is not suitable to use in its treatment things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do that, the disease returns worse than the first; but it works with softening things, such as fenugreek; and the rose water or alum and flaxseed oil are cooked, and applications of dyaquilon founded on one of the eyes, and it envelops a tent, and the treatment of this.

And the treasure of your cure is that you take care to not let it slip according to the form it was in before; and these works that we have said are only addresses of this illness, so it does not relapse according to the form it was in before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is disfigured and truly called "axacrati", and is naturally and accidentally.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and fractures and cautery and similar things; and the way of operating is that you take a needle, in which it has double thread, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pierce through the left arm, as far as the right, so that the thread goes into the head of the flesh; then place the flesh above all the needle, and cover with a spatula large.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the papyrus returns according to what is necessary, it's good; if not, take a razor and put it in the wound, and turn the papyrus, and make two wounds or cuts within the papyrus; and be the heads of the two wounds at the angles of the incision that you have covered, and make one angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is like the figure of a letter which has not "I griesche"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity whose edges are thus disfigured, from what follows the papyrus, then adjust the two separated parts, and sew with a thread of wool; then cure it with what we have said about softening medicines, and tinctures, until it is healthy.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a wound or a break or a cautery, it is necessary that you make a plain wound beneath the hairs of the papers, and according to what is before; then uncover between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters appear to know how to make it return to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what he needs of treatment and of remedies in many different ways.
dou soudement de la papiere	by sudden movement of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this joining has occurred in such a way that the paper above is stuck with the white of the oil, and cannot move or do its natural works, then it is necessary that you put the point of a razor beneath the paper, and lift it up high; and hold as pincers, until you catch what is attached to the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too blunt, so that the patient cannot suffer from the spatula being too sharp or cutting the oil; and make your incision, removing what is assembled, lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and it is all healthy, and never again in the sharp oil, but with gentle lifting, and with a bandage; then put between the paper and the oil a linen tent, and put on the oil a moistened cloth in abundance of water; and after three days use gentle bandages and soothing things as much as possible.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the corner of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the corner is affected in two ways: it is nervous and similar to a hard thick scab, and another which is not nervous, but similar to a pale moist congealed humor, when one touches it with iron and cuts it with pincers, if it cannot be removed; and both appearances begin from the great artery, and gradually increase until it covers the entire sight and light and movement of the eye.

And be careful that the artery does not touch the raw flesh and break it, and that the pruning is not perceived; and after the incision, puts a little of warm broth in the eye, and makes a collyre of litargire, and leaves it until the next day; then cures what is there, as much as it needs to be healthy.

de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye

de l’issue de l’oil	of the exit of the eye

des aigues de l’oil	the eyes of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the similarities of wounds in the division, and that which is necessary to perceive; if one works according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you seat the patient between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and hold the healthy eye firmly; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eyes are left-handed, or in your right hand if the eyes are right-handed; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are left-handed, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eyes are right-handed; then place the point of the instrument beneath the crown by the thickness of a thread in that white part of the eye at the lesser eyelid, then insert the instrument called "almagda" vigorously, and twist your hand until it pierces into the white part of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the clear thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way of almagda be at the forefront of the measure of the spaces which are from the prune up to the end of the blackness; and this is the crown of the eye; if you see the bone in that paper by the clarity of the woven fabric, then place the instrument next to where the wound is, then press it down one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	Let the needle descend now, if the patient sees it before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting a little, and if the needle rises the second way, place the fire with the instrument, and when it is well fixed and does not rise, then extract the Almagda gently while turning your hand slowly and steadily; and then put the needle back in a little of the gemstone, and lift from that eye within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by default the eyes troubled or clouded in oil of roses and in abundance of egg whites, and tie with the healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our kind, put on a common broth with an abundance of egg whites.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the medicine cannot enter the eye due to its thickness, because there are some men who have very hard eyelashes, it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", which is of this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then the conjunctive soulement is pierced, and do not go too deep in the font, but make the subtle eye, then put Almagda, as we have said; and at the completion of the work, appear to the patient the dormeur having a troubled sleep, in which he sleeps on his back in the dark eye; and be aware of all movements, and take light food, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and be bound according to his disposition until the third day; then unbind him in the same dark house, and test his sight, and make him see certain things, and then put him back in his bed until the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you elevate it, because the needle rises hastily.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	Here is the translation:
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then it leaves the house little by little, and converts into its cases; and knows that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in his country they made a certain medicine called "almagda perciet", which drew out the water, but however I never saw any of it in our land, nor did I ever read about it in the books of the ancients; and by chance it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the similarities of the forms of alumga, because those who do not know them go astray; and they should be properly prepared.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And thus the head of the augurs of this same subtlety, and the last one in three angled points.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh over the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes they are born or have diverse chars joined together, because there are some that resemble scorpions with many feet; and if there is such a char with an enchanted fixed color, and if it has a soft char of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of those chars which are soft and not enchanted, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open their nostrils, and throw the onion at those chars, and pull them forth; for you know how to sustain the subtle spatula on one side, as long as you know that this char is entirely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that cannot be coped, open everything .i. of the subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if without swelling, or an abscess forms, drain it as needed; and if it is malignant abscesses, hasten to cauterize until the blood is stanched and all the flesh is burned, then pour in water or vinegar and wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nostrils do not open, and moisture comes up to the palace, know that it is healthy; and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is a char born in the bone above, which the instruments cannot reach: then you must thread a slightly thick linen filament, and be careful with your hands, and hold each end of the space at least; and place the patient's head at the tip of the filament in his nose, and pull it through as it comes out through the nose into the mouth; and many times children are taught thus in schools, and it is an easy thing for one who wants to do it; then hold the head that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and know one after another while being careful as we who have the filament.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do so much that you know the nuts have corrupted that flesh, then draw out the thread, extract the blood, and anoint the thread with Egyptian unguent, and put it back in the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the unguents corrode all that remains of the flesh; and then put a plaster of poultice on the nose for several days until it is healthy, and if there is need of medicines to dry, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, from which they distill the oils and medicines into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or copper, resembling a covered lamp, like a tube, and lead them thus; and if you see, make a close tube, and let the instruments be plain for cleansing the head; and have .i. a holder at the head to hold it when one heats the oil or any liquor.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh over the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a malady called "telul" appears on the head near the nose, and grows and becomes large, until it is visible to behold; and therefore you must cover it at the beginning, and remove all hair, then apply the cautery or burning medicine; and if you delay covering it until it becomes large, take care if it is hard, of dark color, of poor sense: if you do not touch it with iron for it is an abscess that grows inward, because when one covers it many times, great evil comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of dark color, and you see that you can cover it entirely, then the patient will be relieved and the treatment of dry and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is covered and bruised
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when continuous suppurations come in one of these cartilaginous wounds, it profits little, because it often happens in no houses.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary then to wait until it has happened to none, if you see that the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring the two lips together to a suture, then cure until it is healthy; and if the lips are already disjoined on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scrape all the parts of their core until they heal, then assemble the two lips to a suture, and hold them in place, and powder with powder of dragon's blood, and incense broiet; and put on the powders a piece of strong or other suitable plaster, and let it stick by itself, then cure with ointment until it is healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of stitching is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly; or with thread, as I have made you know.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At the hands of men who have dense abscesses on their lips, hard, resembling grains of vezes, and smaller and larger; then it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut into each node, and take them with pincers and cover each part; then apply the liquid after the incision of vitriol broth, until the blood is stanched; and then leave it to heal, and cure the lip of dry things until it is healthy.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a sore appears on the gums where it is attached, which the ancients called "albulus"; if it is necessary to support it with tongs, and apply it to its root, and let the blood or sap flow; then put on top of it vitriol powder, or other drying and astringent powders; and if that sore returns after the incision, and many times happens, so apply it a second time, and cauterize: if it does not return anymore after the cautery; and these are the forms of treatment for covering.
des sordens	of the abscesses
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes abscesses gather at the top of the teeth, deep in the mouth between the gums, ulcers that are wide and tight; and sometimes the black, yellow, and green teeth, as long as the corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth become putrid; if it is necessary to make the patient sit between your hands, and their heads be in your holy, and take out the teeth or ulcers appearing, so that nothing remains; and thus do with the blackness and the greenness, and the yellowness and other stains, as long as they are removed; and if you remove what is at the first root, it is good; if not, then restart on the second day and the third, until you have everything removed; and know that teeth have need of various forms of treatment to be restored, according to what the work demonstrates, because the roots that one removes from the teeth have other forms than those between the teeth; and these forms and others are with you well-prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you delay to treat it as soon as you can, for this should not be done otherwise; for it is a very high substance just up to then so that one has no excuse to delay.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained by two tiring forces, it is necessary that you are certain of the tooth's pain.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and they think it is in a healthy tooth, and makes the good tooth ache; and yet the pain does not depart from that, as long as the bad one is strained, for we have already wanted to do this for these healthy ones; and when you are well certain of the aching tooth, then it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth on all sides with a spatula strongly to ward off the gum from all parts; then move your fingers or subtle tenaculums at first a little and a little, as long as they are well loosened, then hold them firmly in place; and let the head of the patient be in your healthy hand between your knees, and hold it well so it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not come out forcibly, take one of these instruments and gently push it into each part lightly, and remove it as you did at first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the teeth are perceived and gnawed, it is necessary that you fill them with drapels, where the perforations are; and if you hold them subtly in the fastenings, so they do not break while being held; and it is necessary to work very carefully around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And you do well to beware that you do not break it, and leave a part remaining, and reveal to the patient through the wickedness of the root even greater pains than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act thus as the ignorant surgeons, who in their haste and hardness break the cartilage, and do not amend what we have related; but they come often through the obsession of this great disease for the roots that they damage, or for the cartilage that they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is drawn, wash the spot with wine or vinegar and salt; and if blood comes out, which often happens, apply the spot with vitriol powder; and if it does not work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, which you use to extract teeth first, should be long and pointed, with large handles, so they do not slip when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be large limbs so they do not bend in the stretcher, and let them be of iron well made, and let them be tightened by muscles to hold.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root stays behind while pulling, it is necessary that you put a cotton cloth moistened in borax water on the spot immediately.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the joints are softened, then apply the clamps called "algefri", so that the head seems to be in a gentle shape; and thus they are made like a file and that is their form.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these clamps, then you must uncover the flesh entirely around the root, and put in the instrument called "althali", that is to say a scalpel, of which this is the shape.
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and big so that it does not break, and if the root jumps by itself, it is good; if not, then help with all the instruments, from which the forms come here afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps with this instrument that has many grooves, from which the form is:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are in front of the rows of teeth, and of this instrument that resembles large pincers, from which the form is:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And be these instruments strong so that they cannot break, and know that many of the teeth's instruments are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise masters subtly find their own instrument, according to what their work and the illness show them, because there are some illnesses where the ancients did not teach at all about an instrument due to the diversity of wounds, and it breaks or cracks in the cartilage or other bones, or it rots, if one seeks these instruments that they need, which I have told you, and help with the gestures, from which the form is:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be thick and well-gripping to hold the bone, so it does not slip away, but then holds and opens; and then restore to the bone suitable medicines according to that, and if there is porousness in the bone, and it is small, if you take all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not in accordance with the natural body, and its form is ugly, and especially in small women, if it happens that you know the teeth are not after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and one cannot soothe or file: then take the root; and if it is joined with the tooth, take this instrument which has a similar shape, and is like a small beak, and is made of iron sharpened at the tip.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the coping is little by little in the jaws for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, then file it with a similar file as its shape.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file of which one makes the needles; and in filing the tooth little by little in the jaws gently, so that it does not move until it settles; then smooth out the roughness at the end without any rasp, and if the teeth are too sharp and they bite the tongue, if it happens to file the asperity until it is even, so that it does not bite the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth falls out
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth is dislocated, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press on it so that they do not bite, and you have treated them with constricting medicines, but it does not work; if you need to restrain it with a gold thread, because the silver thread turns green and rotten, but the gold one never moves; and let the thread be neither too large nor too small, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you want to adjust the teeth, take the thread and pass it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the head between the bad teeth, if there is one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then recommence the covering up to the part where you started, and hold your hand subtly and steadily, so that it does not move at all; and let your binding be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the heads of the thread to a pair of clamps, and assemble them, and place them between the healthy tooth, and set it so that it does not block the tongue; and then let it be thus straight as long as it can stay, and if it dislocates, or the threads break, if it stays and serves thus all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the adjustment of the two healthy teeth, and the two molars, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, put it back in its place, gradually, as we have said; and do not meddle with those who are not skilled and suffer, and never make the form of a tooth of ivory from a cow, and put it in the place where the defect is, and hold it in place as we have said, and let it stay and serve thus long life.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	from the burning of the thread of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	It never happens that the ligaments which come from under the tongue or naturally, are not thus; or by accidental wound; and the works are such that you open the mouth of the patient, and hold their head in your healthy one, and lift the tongue; then take the nervous thread of a large size, so that the tongue is dislocated from its holding, and if there is hardness or numbness, and it is suddenly wounded, if you anoint with unguent and take the large ligament; and beware that the fissure is not too deep, for the artery which is underneath; and when you have done, lift the lever of warm rose water and of vinegar, or of cold water, then put under the tongue a tent of linen; and bind the patient each night, so that they cannot swallow.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the flow of blood comes, set on the livid spot a warm poultice; and if the wound does not heal, cauterize it with a gentle cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with another treatment until it is healthy.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see the thread of a foul color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is cancer; and if it declines into a whitish color, and there is moisture, then remove the uncleanness, and make a subtle spatula, and deliver from one part and another; and if the blood does not come to your work, put on vitriol bruise as large as it can be stained, then return to your work until you treat everything fully; then lift the water of hay and of seed, and cure with other cures until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there come ulcers in the throat called "godath", and they are properly called "II amandres"; and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they do not heal, beware: if it is a hard abscess with little sense and of foul color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also because of the flow of blood; but let it be until it is ripe, and then you will cut it, where it would break by itself; and if it is of a white color and the root is subtle, prepare the instrument to cover, but first make sure the abscess is calm and at rest.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his head should be healthy, and he should open his mouth and hold the scissors between his hands, and press the tongue underneath to all the instruments, because this is the method; whether it's with silver or subtle copper, as one cuts.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Here is the translation:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, take a candle with tongs, because it is of the same form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be cutting on one part and naming on the other part; and when you have taken hold of one of the embers, take hold of the other in the same manner, and after incision gargle the patient with hot and cold water, and hot and gentle, and if there is evacuation of blood, then gargle the patient with hot water, or scorching pomegranate seeds that are cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the wound is stained; then heal it so it is healthy; and no other abscesses will grow in the throat except for the .ij. embers, if you take hold of them thus like the .ij. embers immediately.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was growing inside her throat, it's known as a small abscess; and I had well pressed close the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the passage that was blocked, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained like that for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had grown so much that it had already put out two roots through the two nostrils of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened to do it then, and inserted a finger into one nostril, then the matter flowed out, and a large portion of pus came out; then I made another insertion into the other nostril, and opened the mouth and pressed the tongue; afterwards I inserted the finger into these abscesses, and cut away a part, and only a little blood flowed out; and thus the passage of the throat was cleared for the woman, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not cease from cutting away at that abscess for a long time; and the abscess recurred again, and refilled the space that I had emptied, so much that it became very large; then I deceived her and cauterized inside the throat: thus she stopped growing worse; and I parted from those parts, and knew only God did something about it after me.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the vein descends to the skin, and it is inflamed and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is grossly swollen and round, it is called an "ulcer".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not profit at all, and you see that the painful abscess is appeased, and it is subtle; then it is necessary to cut into it. And the one that is rounded and not long; and it is blood-red or dark blue or black, then it is necessary to avoid cutting into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary, therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument which we have mentioned before; then prick the vein with a needle, and draw from beneath, and cut into one of the two veins that I have said are suitable for incision of the two handles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the superfluous flesh which is beyond the natural term; for if you cut more, it grieves the voice and the speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two handles, and cure until it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of cutting, it is necessary that you use skill at the cauterization of the senses for fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of burning with the cautery is sharp and keen.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head in your healthy hand, and then presses the tongue to the instrument that we have said or chapter of cautery, and confines with sharp lively heat, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and in applying the movement of this instrument, from which comes the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Here is the translation:
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, not that of cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calament and ysope and origanum and rue and camomile and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them in a pot, and put it thus, and make it boil; and the pot should be well glued with strong earth, and in the pot there is an instrument that cuts according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it is of silver or copper, and one of the heads is thrust into the mouth of the patient as long as the vapor rises to the eye through the cane, so that the eye is mortified; afterwards, it frequently recovers, until the eye dries out, and beware that you do not do this at the beginning of the onset of hot abscesses, for many things happen; and do not do this further than at the decline of hot abscesses.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put a piece of egg white in the head, so that the patient's mouth does not get too hot; for the egg white does not let the vapor bother the mouth, and it is a good remedy altogether healthy.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it happens at the throat or spine of a fish, or anything; so it is necessary that you extract what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you see the thing; and what does not appear to you and is returned to the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit thus, so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps by chance the thing will be expelled through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of turnip, or a root of lettuce, or a crumb of dry bread; and tie the thread to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will stick, and then you will extract further; and if it does not come out from what we have said, take an instrument for extracting according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the curved instrument be at the top of the head so it can enter more lightly into the throat, and hold the head high lifted; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all may go wrong, nor insert it within; and it is worth that the patient inserts the instrument, because it should be inserted or the thing is in vain; if it goes below, where it draws everything equally, as long as it goes equally.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the sensitivity of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	No medicine is suitable for the wound, as I have said in the division, by the treatment of medicines; and when this does not benefit, then look at the patient's throat in the sun, afterwards press the tongue to the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the abscess, if it draws to a small pointed tip, or subtle tendons that hold on to it.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if it does not work, take a hairy thread, and insert it into the patient's throat, then push or withdraw the thread with an iron rod, and make it so often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And prick the patient with water every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full view of cold water, and open the mouth, and throw it in so that it swallows, and move it with your hand often; and if the abscess feels the water, it will burst.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.
