And if it does not burst as we have said, then fumigate the patient with assafoetida, with the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall without tarrying.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot where there are visible coals, and it should be covered with a pierced cover in the middle, and in this pierced one should be the head of the instrument; then you pour out the fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane into his mouth, and closes the mouth, so that the smoke does not escape, but reaches just to the sanies; and the sanies will now fall, and if they do not fall, then recommence the fumigation many times; and suffer the patient thirst, and eat salty and bitter things, and do not drink any water; and then it is necessary that it be done by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument to which one treats the wound, it is, when one can see it, similar to curved tongs entering the throat; and it has the appearance of a beak, and it has roughness of lime, so that what it takes, it cannot release; and see there the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the surgeons of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many abscesses are similar, according to what the memory brings hereafter in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and it is in two manners, one of which is in its own similarity, and because of the moisture it holds.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is through the eyes where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the flesh are different from those that come to joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses that one should not pierce, as long as the bowel is ripe according to its fulfillment; and if there are such that it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their fulfillment, like abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and one lets them be until they are ripe inside, perhaps the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is near a principal member, and you delay the perforation until it is ripe, it will hurt the principal member; or if it is near the foundation, one should pierce it in such a way that it is ripe; and it is not necessary to pierce a ripe abscess without complete digestion, except for one that is near the foundation, so it does not putrefy inside, and becomes fistulous, and cannot be healed in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the signs of the perforation of the abscess which is mortal according to the completion, and it is when the pain is alleviated, and the departure from the fever, and the diminishment of the pain and of the redness, and the soft debating and of the appeasement of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make sit the perforation or more depending on the abscess, and where it appears most; and be the perforation of the long of the body, and if the abscesses are in the hands or feet, or in joints and in the veins and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no putridity.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, one should stretch according to the length of that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the flesh, it is worth more that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed by complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce before that, the body is soon filled with much foulness; and by chance they harden the lips and his inner parts.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there are abscesses that are pierced according to the size of the body, according to what the members have need of.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you make small incisions for small abscesses, small perforations; and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to shave the skin, and cover; when it has become thus like I dress, and is amortized, it is necessary to do as one does for bubbles: and if there are those that are cut into three angles, and if there are those that one covers like the foil of myrtle, as abscesses of the angles; and if there are those where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head, if a superficial abscess forms, it is necessary that you prick it plainly; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has gathered great matter, and you prick it, but do not drain all the matter at once, but rather in part; then stop up the abscess until another day, then drain nothing further; do this many times, little by little, until the matter is all gone; especially if the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman carrying, or small children, or decrepit old men.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the surgeons often fail once with the flow of matter, so that by chance the patient dies, and you do not perceive it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Heal then this chapter with great caution, and when you have pricked your abscess, suck out the wound, and look to see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a plain incision, apply tinctures of flax or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, it is necessary that you put a tent in each one so that they come together; and if you have caught in the abscess a piece of skin, and you have sewn it around, it is necessary that you fill it with much cotton or dressing of flax thread, without moisture, and leave it until the third day; then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it be sound.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if you remove blood which has come to the surface, soothe it with cold and ease, and wipe away the dross, and place a dressing on the surface, repeatedly soothing many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you persist in removing blood, soothe it with governance and care, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is winter, and the wounds or abscesses are very nervous, then you must put on warm tents and soft drapes in wine and hot oil; and if it is summer, and the wounds are inflamed, then you must put on soft drapes in cold water and oil, or in wine and hot oil, just until the third day, as we have said; and then undo the abscess and the swelling and the treatment, as it is fitting, until it is healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: for you have said how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and see here this chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the wounds come from small abscesses, and are ways of knowing that they are in the thigh, just like the sign of a wound, and there is much similarity in it.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There is fat and such things where there is moisture, just like in pulses; and if there are such things that are hard and piercing to the cutter, and there is no doubt that the artery does not act contrary.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the operations of the cutting instrument are that you test all the instruments which are called "entromissoire", because its form comes from this, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, it will be detected by feeling from above the loin.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is evacuated, scrape gently without leaving behind the skin that contains that moisture, for it returns immediately when you leave nothing; then apply cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and in wine, and fill the wound, and leave it until the next day; and this cures what has been wounded at night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then recauterize the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain any longer in doubt; then heal the wound of stitching conveniently, so that it may be healthy.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscesses hold in a thick layer, so shape it according to this form, from a distance; and you throw away the uncleanness, and scrape off everything around, and put all your treatment of drawing out the humor for the skin where it lies; and if the artery makes you do the opposite, so do what I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And thus do with the abscess if it is perforated, and cut and cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut into the perforated abscess and the moist area, it is lighter, for they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if there is no moisture in some of these abscesses or heads where it has not been affected by moisture, and one of these abscesses that I treated was the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and whitish, and could not break it open; and if someone had made a futile effort to do so, they would have done just as much harm as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming from the head, it is necessary that those which come from the heads of children and the roots of the ears, one should operate when they are still very dependent on the brain, because much issue comes out of the bowel; and one should treat them as it is necessary.
des scrophules	of the scabs
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur at the neck, and beneath the shoulder blades, and in the groin area, and never come from another part of the body or limb, and are very large, and are intertwined one with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each swelling is properly located on its side, as the tumor and abscess of the head, as we have said; and the similarities of these swellings are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	in those cases where you see good disposition in the touch, and it is similar to the color of the body, and changes in each part and does not become bitter as it reaches neither the artery nor the conduit, and it is not deep; so it is necessary that you cut into it from above, and scrape away each part, and it stops at the two lips of the heart as onoins, if you are a master, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and you remove little by little, and be sure that you do not touch the nerve or the vein, and do not let the spatula slip, lest your hand falters, and do not see too far ahead, so you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut into the vein or artery, and it does not let you operate, then put on the wound a vitriol ointment, or some powders that staunch blood, and hold the wound steady; and leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound is softened, and begins to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is staunched, return to your work, until you complete it; then examine with your right index finger if there remain small scrophulae, and cut and mend them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrophula, it is not necessary that you cut out the scrophula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall off by itself without harm; then fill the wound with much cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the entire scab, it is necessary that you reassemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, then there will be no more superfluity because of the greatness of the scab.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you understand to cut at the root of it, and draw out strongly, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scabs that hold superfluity, pierce where it appears to die; and pierce thus as was said before, depending on it, then you will mix in ointments and similar things, so that they corrupt what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well purged, if the treatment with ointment brings healing charm, until it is healthy.
de squinance	of scalping
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones said and spoke of the surgery of the throat; but I never saw in our land who did it, and it's the scripture of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have scalping, it is necessary that the partition of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be cut; and one should not help by this, because all the veins and the mouth of the patient are at risk of having an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in the jaws.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the mouth, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to prevent the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary, therefore, when we want to open the epiglottis, that we open it beneath three circles or four with a small opening through, between the two circles or according to the quantity of the opening of the syphac, not in the cartilage; and if this is well suited to the section of the epiglottis, there is no charm, and the vessels are long enough to inquire.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, then it is necessary to stretch the skin of the throat to the entire neck, then cut the vein as far as it reaches the tonsil; and drain the vessels of blood, if you see nothing, and then cauterize the syphac, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the flesh of the tonsil which swells up through the broken vein, and by the deficiency of the voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed from which one doubts the strangulation, assemble the two lips of the wound with gentle care, and sew it all together without touching the cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until it is healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	But beware that one does not do this just then when the throat is completely swollen, and the patient is judged to be at death's door, and lacks breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cauterize on the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death; and for this reason the old doctor orders to leave the wound open as long as the malice of the disease has passed, and it has passed in three days or four. And then they order to sew up the wound and cure, until it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young woman received the cautery, and it was placed on her throat, and part of the sinew of her arm; and I was called to cure her, and found her almost dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had issued from it, and knew well that it had not been properly covered with a bandage or dressing, except for the throat, and the veins were issuing forth through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened, and sewed up the wound, and cured her until she was healthy; and I did not find in the young woman any fever except that she was hoarse of voice, and recovered afterwards to her disposition; for that is why I said that in the tailoring of the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "throat hernia", and it is a large abscess in the color of a jasmine, and it is very common in women; and it occurs in two ways: naturally, and accidentally; or naturally it has no harm.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental is in two ways, one of which seems like a thick node, and the other way seems like an abscess that comes from the artery; and there is fear, and it does not want to open a false passage except in the one that is small, and probes and searches throughout the entire internal passage: if you find it thus as I do not see a thick node, and it does not penetrate any vein, then you cover it, just like one covers the nodes, and draws it out through its entire coif, if there is none; and examines everything well, and cures it as it wants, until it is perfectly healthy.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways of our craft are, which I will describe all the similarities; and now it is necessary that I tell all the differences that exist between them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that the illness is fever and chill, as long as the inflammation has passed, and it is accomplished by the putridity; then the fever and chill are restored.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the patient who has no heat nor fever nor pain, and contains a syrup, which is their own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins thus as a jaundice, and becomes thick; and are according to these similarities, whether grey, or moist, and many colors are so as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the ninth node, that you examine and inquire first about all the instruments which are called "entromissoires", according to what its form will be or chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses in us is that you take or make more moist the place where you find the abscess, and turn your two fingers little by little, until you feel that the instruments have pierced the heart, then according to the size of the abscess; then extract the suppurating matter, and take care that it does not flow out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	Here is the translation:
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if he remains nothing, if it returns to us many times; and if it remains a little, and the wound does not grieve, if one applies some corrosive powders to the wound, and holds the wound steady, and puts on soothing hot applications, and cures other cures until it is healthy; and if it is great, if he cuts the two lips of the wound, and cures what injures within.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein is swollen against the contrary or otherwise, then hasten and apply the liquid of vitriol, and let it stay for two or three days, until the wound suppurates, and restore the ebullition of blood; then return to cauterizing what has been delayed from now on.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of instruments for surgical incisions, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares which are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses of fistula; and they are also like the needles whose points are cut, and are of citrus iron, or of iron, or of silver, and those which are yellow, and are more proven for piercing black pustules; and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the perforations.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the onions are very similar, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if there are onions with two curves in three ways also; and if there are onions with three curves, and they are also of three ways; and if there are onions with two curves, and onions with a single curve only, and they are of three ways; and all this is necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these is cutting, and there are those that do not cut more than one part, from which one scrapes the nails, because one does not touch the vein or nerve; and of these instruments are the small lancets placed in the hands, so that the patient does not feel it at the opening of the abscesses; and they are of three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses them no more than on charnut skin, like legs, arms, and limbs, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling scrapers of fistsices, according to this form, at which one stains blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one places it sometimes at the healthy spot that connects to the veins, and arteries, and sometimes returns according to this great form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Here is the translation:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis. des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the seats
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the seats are a kind of hard scrofula, where there are ribs, and it is because they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who hold moisture must be treated according to this form, from line b to line g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the entire abscess is empty, fill the wound with much cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with ointment to make it healthy.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to scrofula, then do as we have said in cases of scrofula, and if the wound becomes hollow, then apply fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is broken and the skin above it is swollen, then often abscesses come, and also the vein becomes inflamed and develops an abscess; and if you examine it thus, because it is due to the artery, then the abscesses are deep inside; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel the straining; and when it is due to the vein, then it is reasonable to make a diagnosis; and it is foolish to treat this abscess, and also when it is under the seats and the narrow places and in the hollow of the neck and many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then it is necessary to abandon the treatment with iron, and the one who is at the head must abandon also, and in the one who has an inflamed artery, make a perforation above the skin of the loin; then open the incision with onions, and carefully separate the artery from the tissue, so that it becomes uncovered; then put a needle underneath, and make it pierce up to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then touch the place which is between the two ligatures of an intromission, until the blood flows out, and be freed from the abscess; then bring back the treatment which begins with a bougie, so that the ligature holds; then treat what is necessary to reach what is healthy; and if the abscess is due to the incision of the vein, then it is necessary that you hold in your hand what you can of the abscess to the entire skin, then put the needle underneath the place which you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and there is a double thread, so that you pull it from the other side; then touch the abscess as I have told you, or the ligature of one of the two parts with the thread of the filigree; and if you doubt that the thread does not hold, then rebury another needle to the entire thread underneath the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in three places; then cover the abscess until the superfluity flows out, then cover the superfluity of the heart and leave what is tied; then put on a moist dressing with wine and oil, then bring back treatments of tents and ointments until it is healthy.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the kidneys
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Here is the translation:
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And it often happens that the joints and the two toes or all the limbs where there are joints, and it is the painful abscesses, and their color resembles the color of the body, and they are in many dispositions without pain; and when one extracts forcefully, the patient feels pain, and it is not in the depth of the body, but beneath the skin; and it moves well from all parts, and does not go forward or backward, nor beneath nor above, and he who is in joints cannot be covered by iron: by chance it will contract; and he who is at the head or at the forehead, makes the skin on the spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscesses are small, you hold them with pincers, and cover them at their root; and if they are large, you suspend them from the onion-like swelling, and scrape, then remove the bone and assemble the wound to the suture, and cure until it is healthy.
des grosses boces pendans	of thick bulging swellings
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor. I copied them and found in one 18 ounces weighing, and in the other 6 ounces., and the operations in the incision are such that you examine if the patient is moist, and the color of the joint is pale and moist and of subtle root; if you copy at the spatula large, and they are in your presence the fire cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For when the bloodletter comes too frequently with great decorations of blood, and if you do not faint, then hasten to give cautery; and if you see the patient is anxious and afraid of the incision of the iron, take a well-made thread, and tie the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then restrain it, and do not cease from restraining the thread until it touches the joint, and so it does not work; and if the roots are large, fear not to cop at the same time for the belly, but you can well cop half, then cautery so it does not return; then cure the wound, and beware that you do not touch the thigh which is of faulty color and poor sense and little regard.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an encrusted abscess, and I will come to the treatment of encrusted abscess hereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the swelling is full
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	Here is the translation:
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is by the outlet of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses with their fingers if it recedes, and then returns, and sometimes it happens that it becomes narrow, and grows greatly at the entrance of the bath and through strong effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it's due to moisture, it's a light thing, and appears well when you press on it with your hand, it doesn't constrain at all; and if it's due to blood, it appears by these signs: large and hard abscesses, and is fixed according to a quantity; and if it's due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the works are that you examine whether the appearance is due to the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is necessary that you leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in this chapter on abscesses, concerning the artery and vein.
