Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventilations of the sides are worth as much as three veins of the arm, because it attracts blood from these large veins; and instruct the healer that he does not make a cut too deep in front, because the joints are naked of flesh, and know the positions of nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping that is on the back is suitable for hemorrhoids from the bottom, and for diseases of the anus, and it is necessary that the cup be large, and be of copper, so it has the power to treat well; and by chance, if it were subtle, it would break; and it makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cuppings of the legs heal openly, for they attract blood from all over the body, and are suitable for old pains in the kidneys, and in the marrow, and in the bladder, and reset the fluxes; and they are in the place of .ij. sophenes, and of .ij. chevilles, and anyway they restore the body after long use, and bring forth pus in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the cupping is that you put it on first void, and suck moderately, and put it hastily, and remove evenly, and do not cease from doing this, until you see the red and swollen place, and appear the roughness of the blood; then firm, and replace the cuppings, and take care in the disposition of the body, for there are those who have tender flesh, and clear pores: if it is necessary to strike once softly, and necessary to make large wounds, and a little deep ones; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike .ij. times: the first time to subtilize the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the wound is very deep, it is necessary to cauterize three times; and when we want to draw out a little blood drop by drop, then we suffice with a single application.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want to remove a lot of blood, we recommend it often; and if the wound is shallow, we make a cut in front, and the terminations are such that the cauterization should be suddenly perceived, and it is necessary for those who have thick skin and hard, and who have narrow pores, that you anoint the joints with oil of opening and dissolving properties: if it is in summer, of violet oil, or of sweet almond oil, or of cucumber seed oil; and if it is in winter, of cress oil, or of lily, or of chamomile, or other similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is large and cold, take oil of marjoram, or of balsam, or oil of aniseed, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the skin is tender and has large pores, it does not need to be anointed with oil, but rather should be washed after the ventilation of rose water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or water of cucumber, or water of porcelain, or similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, if they rise from aisil, or from water of myrtle, and of sumac, and of similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have gross superfluousness lift themselves with old wine, or water of elder, or decoction of anet or chamomile, or similar things; and it is not suitable to be anointed with a ventouse before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and one should not sleep after the ventilation, and it is necessary that they get warmed up, when they need to be ventilated and when they are ventilated.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware of those who are anointed with choleric temperaments, and their blood is too agitated and inflamed; if it is necessary that they take cold things, such as green apples and endives and lettuce in the shade, and similar things; and avoid pungent foods, and flesh of rooster, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion, if he takes syrup of honey, and wine with pleasant odor, which is between old and new, and eats little, and eats little pieces and small birds and pigeons; and the day he feels wind, he should drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men sometimes triacle or muscat before ventilation, or after, to comfort the principal members; and let the blood be subtle, but it does not matter that those who are hot do not drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cuppings that are applied without piercing are those that are applied to the liver, and to the spleen, and to the podagre, and to the belly and the bowels and the loins and the thigh, because these members do not suffer from being pierced with cups, and it is not done except to attract blood from member to member, as we put them on the arms when they are not healthy; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we put cuppings on the belly and on the bowels to diminish the member; and to remove pain, when there is obstruction or stone, it removes by its attractive virtue by chance the obstruction, or dislodges the stone from its place; and thus it is done when one applies them to the liver and to the spleen when there is retained wind, and these cuppings are administered empty for sucking so strongly; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes plain hot water, as in illnesses of the pleura, and in such a way that one fills the cupping with hot water or water in which herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass administered with fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it should be two inches and a half palm's width from the fontanel, and it should be placed on the side next to the millet, like a small hole, as if to insert a needle, and it should be of iron or steel, to put a staple in, and it should be wide and narrow according to the diseases and the age of those who take them; for the ventouses of children are different from those of the old, and of the lean from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And it should be placed thus, this ventouse on the limb: take the staple of wax or linen, and put it in the ventouse across the rod that is in the ventouse, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the ventouse lest it burn the patient; and then place it on the limb, and the two should be on the small hole as we said, so that when one wants, if the vapor goes out, and remove the ventouse; and take the linen thus beforehand, and reapply often, if you have mastery.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping device which is administered in disease of pleurisy, at every ailing point, it has no edge nor perforation, and it is not administered except when it is full of water, and it is placed on the limb just so; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Cupping devices are not administered except on members where you cannot put cupping glasses because of their smallness, such as eyelids and gums, and similar places; and in the naked flesh, such as fingers or toes, and similar things; and the quality of the usage is that when you find cupping devices that are in sweet and clear waters without purge, take them; and put a nut in sweet water, so they become familiarized, and have nothing in their belly; and then be careful with vein and cupping device, then rub the limb until it becomes red, and put on the cupping devices; and when they will be full, and attract, that is where you can put the cupping device, put it, for it is worth much afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	Here is the translation:
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the sinews do not want to take, rub the vein of fresh blood with a needle as long as the sinew is in it, and then put them back, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will adhere; and when you see that they stick, powder on a little bit of aloes and of crushed brook, or of cinders, so they will hold now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is restoration of fracture and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the foolish people are ignorant of this chapter, for they did not find anything in the ancient books, nor did they read any letter; and for this reason the science is strange in our land, because I did not find any good; and I do not know anything, except by the science of the ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the experience of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and I have summarized it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of instruments that are prepared, as I did in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the word and the chapters where the wise men put their understanding, and they stay on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when breakage or dislocation or twisting or bruising occurs to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient from one side and another, so nothing touches them completely, if they are weak in body, or old, or feeble; or if their tension is not very strong, or too cold; and moderate cold joints, it means to know cold foods, and flesh of capon and goat, and do not drink any wine, and do not eat coarse rough fish, and do not fill themselves too much with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of hot abscess, nor spreading of matter in the limb; if the patient returns to their first government that they had used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to restore, it is necessary that you nourish the patient with meats that make great nourishment, or they have viscosity, just as fermenting in water, and rice, and bread, and feet, and pork of a cow, and eggs, and fresh fish, and old wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For a suitable nourishment represents muscles and more quickly repairs the break.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well repaired or rejoined according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor those which are too tender, like the bones of small children; but there is no cure, reset on the broken bone a large bandage that holds and joins the limb together, until it strengthens as it was before; and do not touch them at all with their own work, and therefore it is necessary to nourish them with thick meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	Here is the translation:
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if you break with a wound, and break at all a small notch.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And in each manner he has his engine, and his proper instrument for restoration, according to what the remembrance brings into its place; and it is known that the break of the bone occurs when the bones are twisted, and appears well by palpation, and sounds upon pressing with the hand; and when there is no tortuosity in his touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no point of break; but he can have tortuosity, or fissure, or small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It does not matter if you move the limb, but apply the medicines that come here afterwards, and then hold it steady subtly now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the break which goes to the joint, and are the two disjointed parts, they must now be put in equal alignment, so that abscesses do not form; and if abscesses form, let it not bother him for a day, until the abscesses are calmed; then set it in the softest possible way, and know that the restoration of this is easier than the restorations of one who has pieces; then hold steady, as it must be afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, whether it's of two parts, whether it's a hand or foot, or with your hand if it's a small limb, or with two cords, or with a cord and your hand; and put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parties of the broken member are disjointed, you reset them by all means in their places as much as you can, and take care that through your work no harm or injury comes to the patient; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels well in his hand if it seems to him that it is not well: if you straighten it nicely, and do not strain it too much, nor press as those who make it come by their work on the aposteme abscess and contraction of the limb, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in a point, reprimand the patient well so that they do not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor while turning, nor in another way; and take care that the limb is so secured that they feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when they feel no pain, it is not in a point, and you must put it in such disposition that they feel no pain; and take care that it is set straight, so that twisting does not come when it is restored; and the quality of the broken member is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and greatness and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Here is the translation:
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is a swelling or abscess, put on it an aposteme-reducing hot application, and remove the swelling, and let it be thus for some days; then hold steady your esteles, and be in the middle of a large cane reed, or a staff made from a tree, or a palm branch, and be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the estele which one puts on the fracture be a little bigger and wider than the others; and be as long as it is necessary for the smallness or greatness of the limb; then hold steady your esteles as you have done at first, then tie above with a thread conveniently, just like in the first layer on the fracture; the tighter it is, the less; and it is necessary that the thread be moderate, not too big nor too small, and be of linen thread; for if the threads are big, as I have seen the foolish ones who make their layers of twisted cord, and it's a great error, because the layer cannot be even if it's too subtle, and it doesn't matter that there is less than two fingers' width between each estele.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patients are wounded by the staples of the stiles after the constriction in their healthy places, then put under them swabs of linen or a piece of parchment, so that it does not become inflamed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the breakage, and the courses are broken, I will tell you the treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And beware that it does not suit to strain these broken members on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	Here is the translation:
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way to restore bruising and dislocation and twisting: take absinthe and ladanium and enula and asafoetida and Arabic gum and mugwort, an ounce; myrrh and aloe, an ounce; alechil, eight ounces; and make into powder, and mix with egg white; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and benefits many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of applying plaster that is good for twisting: take mugwort and vismalve, in the shape of an X; mix and blend, in the shape of VIII; add acaice VI; boil Armenian bole X, and crush well, and mix with water or abundant river flow, and apply the treatment.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way of applying plaster to joints and to the bones dislocated from their places, and to alleviate the severe pain, and the usual size of the bone, and the fracture: take new flax, and grind it into a fine powder in a warm oil, and put it on the wound.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore fully, but they are good for alleviating hot abscesses, and properly relieving the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way of plaster that restores broken bones: take dried fig tree leaves, and earthy peony leaves, and crush them together, and make into a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way of applying plaster for the restoration of the bone fracture and to reduce the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Here is the translation:
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to treat more forcefully than the first, when the abscess becomes hard as it comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of vimalve, and seeds of flax, baluster, melilot, and sanucus, and flowers of violets and chamomile, each one part; and crush, and mix with water of salt, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hypocras states in his book that one should not put anything on a broken limb to restore it except for cerote made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and he says that it should be between two extremes, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems according to Galien that one should put on a broken limb, to restore it, warm dry things, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to apply that is good for a wound and pain: take mugwort and leaves of decapitated omes, or feathers of a bird, and vismalve, and make it equal, and pound, and make an application on the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen it a little afterwards, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor is the bone of its place; if you do not loosen it for many days. And if pain comes to the limb, or inflammation, without rest or swelling, hasten it, and loosen it, and remove the dressing now; and take a lighter bandage, and a sponge of seawater, and dip in water, and lift up the limb, until the inflammation ceases, and the pain is alleviated. Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on a dry linen cloth, moistened with rosewater or oil, and bind it on a nut, until you are certain of a hot abscess; and relieve the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then recommence the subtle treatment, and a little dressing, and do not strain it too much as before; and subtly treat it until it is healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that abscesses, swelling, and pain and inflammation are all gathered there, and you have the task of cleaning and binding, then restart, just as you did first equal treatment.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the limb as we have said, do not dislodge it further until after three days or four or five or seven; and never leave it for twenty days, according to what one sees, until the bruising ceases, and approaches the adjustment of the flesh on; then restrain more than before, and the swelling goes down, as I have said before; and if you see the limb dry out more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come; therefore apply hot water therapy every time you dislodge it, and let it be each day, and ease the ligature a little; by this work then the nourishment comes to the limb, and quickly ends what the foolish doctor does, who twists the limb wrongly: it is bad, and these are perilous works, and I do not see anything else but to let it heal and open properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many types of fractures, and various shapes, and the causes are distinct; for there are fractures that are made from a blow with a spear, and the neck breaks all the bone just up to the socket which is beneath the bone, if it is done by a hook or a bar; and therefore this type of fracture is called "hook fracture".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword cuts the bone from above, piercing senselessly, and this type of breaking is called "absolute"; and it is the wound of these two breakings, great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded fracture, or crack, or break of stone, or fall from stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating wound, which approaches just to the membrane that is under the bone, or it is on the bone, and this is a wound or large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound that is implanted in the bone as subtly as a small notch, and the crack is small, and therefore this fracture is called "capillary"; and if the wound that is made by striking with a stone, or falling, or similar thing, and makes the piece of the bone enter below, and the joints are damaged just like the craftsmen do when they strike on the anvils; if between the stone within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And it happens more often to those who have moist bones, like the head of a child; and it has all these types of fracture where small pieces are dislodged, as if they were torn apart; and I will speak of them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all ways of fractures by the withdrawal from them, and the inquiry into their nature, and by the corrupt flesh that is on them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The similarity of the fracture is known by this: when one discovers the bone, and one feels it with the finger, then the black fracture appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, beware of accidents that harm the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and stretching, and palpitations, and fever with chills, and eyes issuing forth and reddening, and other similar things in more dispositions, if it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a disastrous accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the numbness comes to you first, and it is in winter, then you should open the vein before the fourteenth day of the month that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to open the vein before the seventh day, lest the vein under the vein be corrupted, and come the accidents that we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the break of the bone reaches just to the membrane that covers the brain, it is necessary that you divide the affected part thus: and it is that you take hold of the head of the ailing patient, and uncover above the bone in all the ways that you can, and above the shape of the wound more subtle than you can, and if blood comes to discover the bone, or an abscess falls, it is necessary that you use what is needed, and it is that you fill the hollow of the drained drapery with rose oil; and make repose the wound until the abscess is appeased, and be assured of the cessation of blood; then begin on the bone to open, and it is done according to two ways of work: one way is that you cut straight in front, and it is the form.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I make another cut, a larger one than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have a number of diverse surgical instruments, some being straight and others large, and are pointed, and are made of iron indeed; and work lightly, so you do not blister the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and hard, it is necessary that you pierce around it, thus you must minister instruments with caution, not too deeply so they do not penetrate beyond the bone of the entire body, and should have a margin or circle above the point, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you need to have more, if each one comes into its place in the thickness of the bone, so you have instruments for every test; and this is the form of the three manners of instruments.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality of piercing around the broken bone is that you put an instrument on the bone, and turn it with your fingers until you feel that the bone is pierced; then reposition the instrument a little further away, and do so all around, then make incisions in the space of the bone which is between the parts, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you extract the bone with your hand, or with any of the instruments that you hold, such as pincers; and beware that you do not touch the brain or the vital organs.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone, and cut, it is necessary that you remove the aperture which remains of the bone to all other instrument similar to an incisor, but it is necessary that it be more tender and more subtle than the other incisors; and if there remains nothing of the small bones, no splinters, they should lightly hold onto one of the instruments; then cure the wound with tinctures and ointments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is what Galen says, which is more wise; and he praises it greatly, and that's his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you discover a part of the bone, there where the fracture appears, so that when you have discovered that part, you will put beneath the head of this lens-shaped incisor, whose shape is this:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one part, and the affected area is on the II costal, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer above, so that you gently coppice the entire bone around, and take good care of the membrane that is beneath; if it is attached to the bone, so lift it gently, for one lifts it well without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce up to the membrane, and the bone is broken so subtly above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to remove that roughness, and to scrape off the scales with a subtle rasp which you must have in various quantities, to prepare each place most conveniently, according to the work and the figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you rasp before with large rasps, and then with more subtle ones, and do not cease from doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other delicate hair-like fractures and subtle breaks, it is necessary that you prepare the cause according to its adjustment; and this is a thing that is not easily responded to by one who has put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the wound is uncovered, then it is necessary that you apply a bandage of linen, according to the quantity of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another doubled bandage in II or III, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first bandage; and make it as light as possible, so you do not irritate the wound, then administer above another thread, and do not constrict it more than necessary to hold the wound sufficiently; and leave it thus for a day or two, until the apostemes are appeased, then remove it, and administer medicines such as radix of lily, and farina of veins, and powder of incense, and aristologe, and similar things; and make powder from these things, and place on the wound, and administer gentle medicines without irritation; and ensure that the wound is sufficiently clean, so you do not leave the swelling, nor leave it to gather pus, for when pus gathers on the membrane of the brain, it corrupts and putrefies, and brings great harm to the patient; for when you apply something irritating on the wound, it becomes necrotic above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Here is the translation:
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there comes a crisis that occurs due to the medicine that one has applied, which has such a virtue, then it is necessary that you take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and glue them together in the drapet, and put them on the syphac; then one cures in many ways of cures as it is convenient, until it is healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that no time are broken the three parts of the nail above, or one part by the swelling, for these are three bones; and the cartilage below is not broken, so it does not make a wound or twist, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then it is necessary that you put your small finger or pertus dou neis, and match this breakage within your index finger, and at the pouchet by default, until the nail regains its natural shape; and do this lightly, and beware that the patient does not feel pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nail, and cannot be straightened to its place, then it is necessary that you set it even at the head of a slightly thick vein.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the breakage is of two parts, do it in the same way, and hasten to restore the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth, when the aposteme's heat is appeased, then put on the head of the nail tentes of drapelz of linen, if the breakage is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Where you apply it on one side, the break is there; and let the bandages be as thick as they fill the holes of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say that one should soften the tents in mud, and move each joint daily.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary that they be softened with a concoction of egg white and powder of millet; then leave the tents, until the bone is firm, and the cartilages hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes apply egg whites to the nose instead of bandages, and if there is a swollen drapery within, and it holds the break, and soothes the patient within; or do as you have seen.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the nose while you are observing, if you apply cerote or moistened cotton in rose oil, or in a little bag of dyacilion.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come, put an emplaster made from flour of sisament and powder of incense, mixed with egg white, then apply light poultices, and do not bind them tightly; and if the breakage of the knee is small, and it is broken into small pieces, remove the extraneous fragments comfortable to the skin, then sew up the fissure, and treat the painful things in a char, and suddenly, as you apply emplasters and ointments comfortable to the skin; and if there is no inside wound, treat the tents, and put on compresses of lead, until it is healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken apart, and there is no wound in the forehead, and the break is apart so gently, and it is not broken in two, except for the little fragments within, if one recognizes it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the break is in the right part, that you put your right index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the break is in the left jaw, then put your right index finger, and gently adjust the break within, and hold it with the other hand from above, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jaw is dislocated in two, then it is necessary that you administer extension in two parts, so that they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth are moved out of place, or broken, then strain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, and put it on the broken jaw, and put on a double layer; and put on the layer a large, well-made staple, or a piece of even, long and broad leather according to the jaw, and tie it to the mouth that you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then dislocate it on the third day, and then reset to the point where it changed; and apply a poultice made from powder of mill flour with an abundance of egg white or wheatmeal, after you have removed the crust; and apply a light poultice, and if the poultices are effective, and the disposition of the patient does not change, let it be until it is healthy; many times it is healthy in eight weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses or ulcers come, then manage them as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, reset the broken bone in its place; if you subtly remove the excess bone with suitable instruments for that.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it with a flame according to the necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you will have gathered all these pieces, and it does not stay in place, if the wound is large, put there suitable dressings to heal the flesh, so that it be healthy.
de la forcele	of the strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The strength breaks many times beforehand, near the shoulder, and the break is in three ways: either it is broken and dislocated in two, and there are pieces, and it is easier to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operations are when the break is without a wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the shoulder that feels the strength broken; and the other stretches the neck towards the part; then put equal breaks on both sides, so that the form be as it should, and there is no appearance nor movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you have mastery of extending further, set beneath the shoulder of the patient a round sphere of cloth or leather, and let it be thick according to your need; and hold and lift the force with effort, and hold the sphere with your hand, so that you make equal the break, as it is necessary.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the forceps at the defect, because it comes in profundity, so it is necessary that the patient girds around his shoulder, and sets beneath the shoulder a little pillow, and bends the ministers to the shoulder below, until the bone of the forceps is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then adjust the break to your hands, and if you find the debris scattered, so it is necessary that you bend over; and draw forth the lighter pieces, and if the bone cannot join due to any excess movement, so take one of the incisors that you have; but set beneath the forceps this instrument, to guard against excessive movement.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it seems a spoon, and is not a chess, and be as large as the hollow of the bone and the power of the vein; and have two heads, as you see, and one is large and the other narrow, like the routing of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of a hot abscess, cut into the wound, and if the routing is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, fill the wound with drapes and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if the hot abscesses come, then soften with a dressing of rose oil and in vinegar and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The strapping of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cutting, is that you put on the bone the plaster of powdered millstone and egg whites, and apply light poultices, and put a spear-shaped dressing underneath, so you have mastery; then take a very large bandage of a palm's width, then put double-layered poultices, and the plaster; then take a subtle thread of three fingers' width and length, and wrap it around that bandage, so the head of the bandage hangs down; and apply the thread to the fracture, and turn the bandage around the neck, and underneath the healthy joint, and underneath the diseased joint; and reset each part, and when you see that the ligature holds the fracture firmly, and you clearly see that the thread does not move on the fractured bone, so reward it every day, and when the ligatures are relaxed, restrain it; and make the patient lie on his back, and put a small pillow underneath the joint, to lift the shoulder high; if you lighten the fracture of the arm by lightening the shoulder, or you bind the arm to the neck, and no bad accident happens, until 20 days; then recommence the plaster, if you see that it is needed, and restrain it and leave it thus, until it is restored; and it is restored in at most 28 days, and in fewer than any homes.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Here is the translation:
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone protrudes beforehand, and not beneath the heart, if they make it thus, and the bone, and do as we have said in the breaking of the force to appease an abscessed swelling.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the fist
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is sometimes broken in a thousand ways, but this happens rarely; it often breaks at the fracture.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken within, it declines to the lowest point, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks strength, and becomes pale, and sometimes vomits blood, and opens the channels in the broken bone, and the sensation is not good.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their back, and you put a cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and assemble the ribs with your hands, and subtly arrange to make it even in all ways that you can, so that the shape of the bone is as it should be; then put on emplasters and stoups of subtle salt, or another light plaster, and envelop it in a drapery, and tie it around the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turn the round ligament to the back, and hold it firmly, and reward each hour the bandage, and if it becomes loose, restrain it; and if you see it becoming dislocated, through corrosion or pruritus that comes from the blood, or pain or abscess, hasten, and loosen, and remove the emplaster, and address what has come in ways of cures; then restore the emplaster, and hold it as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure des costes	of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	It is known that the fracture of the ribs occurs only in the large ones at the back, and inside the chest, and does not bend except because they are cartilaginous; and one feels it well by palpation with the fingers.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the resetting is that you make the fracture even, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and hold it with a bandage, so you have mastered it.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs declines inward, the patient feels very great pain and piercing, just as if from a thorn, because the bone touches the membrane; and there is numbness, and all at once and vomiting of great abundance of blood, and it is a grievous wound, and the old men have put great ingenuity.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that they need to administer foods that inflate the stomach, in order to soothe the rupture at the weakest point.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, because hot abscesses do not come to life, if they have not developed.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has developed, then it is healthy.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that some of those who put ventouses on the limb, in order to suck out the putrid matter, and it seems like a reasonable thing; however, there is doubt that the ventouse does not attract the superfluous humors from the limb due to the weakness of its disposition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they direct that one should cover the limb of a wounded thigh with hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to make equal the length within, then it should be cured by the treatment of pleurisy, of meat and of medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear through the bone that touches the fabric, and doubt is in the patient, then it is necessary to break above the broken rib, and it is necessary to put underneath the instrument to protect the accumulation; and then one must cut into the bone, and draw lightly, and then sew together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and apply layers of plasters, until they are healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come, put moist drapels on them in rose oil, and apply it to the affected area; and treat thus the area of those that need an abscess, and be gentle with suppurating wounds on the side where it should, until they are healthy.
de la brisure dou col	of the breakage of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes the breakage comes to the bone of the neck, and little by little it grows; and thus has the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when it happens to anyone, and you want to know if they will be healthy or not, take heed if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and they cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many dispositions, and if they move and feel well when they are restrained and not, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient's illness is cured, so one can put a cure.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things come to the spine of the back, and you want to know if they will be healthy or not, take heed if the feet are softened, and if the accidents that are in their hands, and on the back there is windiness and involuntary evacuation; and when one has evacuated on their belly, then there is involuntary evacuation.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is swooning on his back and wants to sit up, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal: do not labor in vain in his care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to them, it is the thing most lightly.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you warm them if there is a hot abscess, apply to the spine oil of rose or oil of musk deer, so it may be appeased; then put on one of the comfortable and soothing plasters, and bind with a ligature, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that side where they feel pain, until they are healthy.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bone is dislocated, it is necessary to cover on the heart; and remove the bone, then reassemble the .ij. levels of the wound, so it is large, with a bandage, then apply the ointment in January, until it is healthy; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the kowe", take your pouchet with your left hand, and put it equally with your right hand on your poitrine, then put the plaster and stick it on, so you have mastery; then hold fast, and if there is a dislocated bone, make it so, and remove it, and cure the wound until it is healthy.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the bone of the hip
