Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the gilbositeit that comes to the front of the foot, there is no one who can heal it; and also the one that comes directly to the ribs, and one cannot cure those except the one that properly comes to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient should be extended on their face in a straight line, and have their spine stretched out from underneath them, so they do not become crooked; then fix the stick at the top firmly on the ground, and another at the foot, and tie a bandage around the affected areas of the patient, and another at the thighs, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two ministers know how to bind the sticks, one at the top and the others at the feet, among the two sticks; and they should be well fastened, the stick as we have said, and the doctor puts their palms on the spine firmly, until they recover.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this treatment, take a three-foot-long tubular device, and place its end below the patient's back, and the patient is in a stable position, and insert the head of the tubular device below the patient's back, then put the middle of the tubular device on the spine; and put the mirrors at their ends on the other head of the tubular device, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see, do it with the tourniquet that turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And it is that you fix two clamps at the head of the patient's arm, and two others at their feet, and between each clamp, above and below, a long span of space; and in each clamp there is a hole, where the tourniquet passes, and the clamps are firmly on the ground, so they do not move; and between the two clamps there is one turning clamp, where the rope turns, and there are two small turning clamps of a long span, to turn the tourniquet; and then you fasten the rope that is among the supports to the tourniquet at the head, and the other rope to the feet at the other tourniquet, and each of the ministers turns their tourniquet to all the rope, and the masters put the spine straight as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, put a scalding plaster with abundant egg white, and then the poultices, and then a tablet of three inches long, which will correct the curvature of the spine and the healthy part of the vertebrae, then tie it with a bandage, as we have said, and use subtle nourishment to heal the patient; and if anything comes at the end of health, it is necessary to administer soothing medicines and rubbings, with the tablet that we mentioned before; and do not give a piece of lead, and do not let the appearance in the rear vertebrae come back, and think that it is dislocation; and it is the bone that opens, for which one must not have pride: perhaps death will come by chance.
des dislocations de la hainche	of the dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	You know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only come to dislocations suddenly, not as with other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated in four ways: inward and outward, forward and backward; and more inward it slips, and a little dislocates forward and backward.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation is that when one joins the injured leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and opens more the injured knee than the healthy one, and the injured one cannot bend its knee at the fire; and it is the limb which is weakened by an abscessed swelling, because the head of the thigh comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the signs of the one who comes to the doctor, if it is that this accident is contrary to those beforehand.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of the one who comes beforehand, if it is that they support their leg according to the accomplishment; however, do not double the knee without pain, and if you want to make it move, then it cannot go forward, and it retains its urine, and inflates the groin, and when it goes, then it passes above the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of the one who comes behind, if it is that they cannot stretch their knee, nor double, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and it is the head of the thigh at the place beneath the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The reminders of this similarity of dislocation are that you should beware that the dislocations are ancient, and they remain according to their disposition, if there is no cure; and it does not seem that it has a presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in that case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is of three manners of dislocation, if you hasten to turn the joint, and strengthen it within and without, and move it straight and crooked; by chance if it returns, and there is no need for another cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, then it is necessary that you strongly hold the limb in one hand at II hands, or at the thigh where it is tied; and another minister stretches his hand over it in such a way that he puts his hands under his haunches, then holds with a soft thread on the hip; and another pulls the head of the dislocation; and they stretch above and below all at once, so that the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four similarities, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it's good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If it does not, then it is necessary to put a cure in its semblance. When the dislocation is in the buttocks, then it is necessary that you place the patient on their healthy side, then put the thread at the root of the hip, and the limb that is under the groin, then stretch the thread above towards the groin, and towards the strength; then take another minister's arms, and embrace the large limb of the dislocated hip, and stretch it to its proper form: if it will return to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot set it in this manner that we have said, then it is necessary that you bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong soft cord above the two heels and above the two knees, and let the affected leg be extended two fingers more than the other; then let it be suspended from the top of a stick, and let it be on the ground two arms' length away; then instruct the servant to wrap the top of the thigh, and let another servant hold with the patient, who wraps around the thigh firmly, because the joint returns quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is in the hip, you should adjust the patient as we have said in the one who has gout, and pull the cord properly on the affected leg, and on the foot also; then place two sticks, one at the top and another at the feet, then fix one stick between the thighs of the patient in the form; and have placed moist drapings around, so that it does not harm the patient, then each servant stands opposite him, and the doctor puts his hand equally on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place on the table, and press as we have said in the gibbosity, and guide the patient onto the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to stretch the sick leg hastily, and according to what I have said; and place the mirrors of pain on the angle of the sick leg, then press with the other hand, and extend below towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is downward, do not extend the patient's leg downward, nor lift it to the ground, but rather make it just as if the hip were dislocated upward, as we have said about lying on the two hips; and place it on its face, and extend the bandage as we have said before, and press on the joint at the table; and it will be fine when the patient extends their legs, and they will be even; then join the thighs, and put the dressing, and bind with a ribbon, so that the hip does not move; and rest for three or four days, then remove the dressing, and put it back on; and if you see that they are even, bind as before, and leave for three days; then remove, and make them walk comfortably, until the limb is comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knees are dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inward, forward, and backward; and do not dislocate at all in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his knee to his thigh, and if it does not adhere to his thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg as he can, and put your back against his face, and put your foot against his feet; then take his knee in your hands, and draw between your two, then bend the two sides of the knee firmly; and another minister extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the signs are that it adheres well to his thigh lightly; and apply the poultice on top, and adjust the leg to the thigh, and bind them together strongly for three or four days, then unbind; and do not trouble the patient further, until the limb is comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not at all, if strong administration is extended, as we have said in the treatment of the thigh, until it be healthy.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the ankle
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The ankles are sometimes swollen, and sometimes entirely dislocated, and inwardly and outwardly.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the flesh is swollen, and it tends towards the part where it is dislocated: the reduction is easier, and one must extend it gently with their hands when it is slightly inflamed.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is entirely dislocated, one must make the patient sit upright, and pull the ministers strongly by the leg, above the flesh; then pull the foot to you with your right hand, and then with the left hand twice, then extend it upwards, and put the foot well upwards; and do this twice, as we have said, in pulling and extending the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, start the work again, for it returns; and if it cannot return thus, make the patient sit on his back on the ground, and fix the passage firmly on the ground between his thighs, and wrap the drapels around, so that it does not escape; then pull the ministers by the thigh, and another minister extends the foot to their hands or to the lien, so that it is above the ankle of the foot; then extend each minister equally, and the passage is thus between the thighs of the patient to hold the dislocation in place; then put the mirrors equally on the dislocation with your hands, and another minister pulls the healthy leg from below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is at a point, set the plaster and bandages above, and hold strongly, and bind the foot to the leg, and wrap the veins that are on the back of the knee, so the ligaments are not too constricted; then leave it for two or three days, and if the ligaments soften, hold strongly; then release it on the third day or the fourth, and allow the patient to walk for four days; and if it proceeds beyond this term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come to the spot, it is necessary that you touch them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healthy.
des dois	of two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the fingers are dislocated, it is necessary to stretch them nicely without effort, and it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any of the two legs, it is necessary that you make the patient sit on a flat surface or on a straight table, and put your foot on what opens from these joints, then press your foot firmly, until it returns; and when it is even, and there is no gap, set under the sole of the foot a table at two heads, then hold strongly, and leave for three days, then release; and make them rest, until they are healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times the patient dies: if you are not presumptuous in the cure, be wise in the art and have long experience, and be pitiful and merciful and tardy, not hard; and use gentle things at the beginning of hot abscesses, and leave the patient in God's hands, if you do not see hope for health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, so that the abscesses do not come to life; and when the limb is in its place, then use gentle things for hot abscesses, and cure the wound, as it is necessary, with dry bandages; and if with dislocation there is a break, and you find less difficulty, then set the bones, and do what we have said about simple illnesses; and beware of entering into fear, according to what I have said, for it will be of no value to you, according to your Creator, and for the safety of your arm and body.
